  <raw>Toyota-GM joint venture in California to implement furlough plan



Mar. 6--NEW YORK -- United Auto Workers members at a joint venture between Toyota Motor Corp. and General Motors Corp. in California have approved a furlough proposal from management, Toyota officials have said.

The union members at New United Motor Manufacturing Inc. in Fremont, California voted 86.5 percent in support of the proposal, which requires them to take Fridays off without pay, the officials said.
The furlough, effective from Friday through Aug. 7, is part of a work-sharing program Toyota earlier decided to implement at some North American factories to protect jobs amid production cuts due to dwindling sales.
The factory was an old GM one that first opened in the early 1960s. It reopened in 1984 as a joint venture of the two carmakers.
Toyota's new car sales in the United States fell nearly 40 percent in February from a year earlier while GM recorded a 53 percent year-to-year fall in the same month.
To see more of Kyodo News International, go to http://www.kyodonews.com Copyright (c) 2009, Kyodo News International, Tokyo Distributed by McClatchy-Tribune Information Services. For reprints, email tmsreprints@permissionsgroup.com, call 800-374-7985 or 847-635-6550, send a fax to 847-635-6968, or write to The Permissions Group Inc., 1247 Milwaukee Ave., Suite 303, Glenview, IL 60025, USA.</raw>
